Everything you list under \"Annual Goals\" is a big-ticket item, and you should list things in order of importance.\n\n- **Monthly Goals**: You define your monthly targets, and finally, break those into specific weekly tasks.\n\n- **Weekly Goals**: After you're done filling out your monthly goals, apply the same philosophy to your weekly goals by asking what you have to do each week this month in order to put you on track to hit your monthly goals.\n\n## Activities and Alignment\n\nMonthly targets should be tied to each strategy (e.g., \"send 300 postcards,\" \"book 4 listing appointments\") with weekly tasks that keep you on track (e.g., \"call 10 past clients,\" \"schedule open house\").\n\nYour weekly goals (activities) should account for your monthly goals (activities), which should in turn account for your annual goals, and if you truly listed everything in order of priority, then your top weekly goal should correspond with your top monthly goal, which should in turn correspond with your top annual goal.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"75d6bd53-b4ff-4c44-92fa-f577747cfeb6","timestamp":"2026-03-07T02:41:49.024Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"81d6966f-375b-45a6-bc10-4435eafa905b"}

Your gross revenue (your GCI) is driven entirely by this chain reaction of productivity, which flows from leads through appointments to closed sales.\n\n## Three Drivers of the Economic Model\n\nThe three drivers are: (1) Leads to Appointments - Generating leads and converting into Buyer and Seller appointments; (2) Appointments to Signed Agreements - Using appointments to secure clients with a signed service agreement; and (3) Agreements to Closed Transactions - Serving clients and facilitating a closed transaction.\n\n## Conversion Rate Structure\n\nThe model uses specific conversion rates:\n- Seller Listing Appointments convert at 80% to Seller Listings Taken, and Buyer Listing Appointments convert at 65%\n- Seller Listings convert to Sellers Sold at 65%, and Buyer Listings convert to Buyers Sold at 80%\n\n## Reverse Engineering Formula\n\nTo identify how many people you need in your database: (1) Goal GCI ÷ Average Commission = # of Deals Needed; (2) # of Deals Needed ÷ Opportunity for Conversion (6.37%) = Minimum # of Contacts Needed; (3) Minimum # of Contacts ÷ Your Conversion Rate = Expected # of Contacts Needed in Your Database.\n\n## Fundamental Economic Formula\n\nIf you desired to have a Net Income of $500,000, your GCI would equal $500,000 ÷ .416 which equals $1,201,923. Here's a walkthrough of the key steps:\n\n## Mike Ferry Listing Presentation Steps\n\n### 1. Opening/Positioning\nThe presentation begins by telling the seller that \"at the end of my presentation tonight one of three things will happen: you'll have the opportunity to list your home with me, or you'll decide not to list your home with me, or I'll decide not to take your listing\".\n\n### 2. Qualification Review\nThe agent quickly reviews questions asked during the initial phone call: where they're moving, why they're moving, when they need to be there, what price they'd like, what they owe on the property, and whether they were planning to sell it themselves.\n\n### 3. CMA Presentation & Pricing Strategy\nThe agent explains that the purpose of the Comparative Market Analysis is to determine the value of the home in the eyes of a buyer. Buyers determine value through comparison shopping, looking at the price based on features and benefits compared to similar homes that have sold recently or are currently on the market.\n\nThe script moves on to a detailed presentation of the comparative market analysis and explains the pricing strategy, methodically walking the seller through the process so they're more likely to arrive at a similar conclusion as the agent did.\n\n### 4. Preparation Materials\nA complete CMA with the suggested price goes in a packet sent in advance, along with a completed net sheet showing all the costs involved in the commission and what the seller will net at the end.\n\nA completed contract goes in the packet, with Mike recommending having the seller sign the paper copy when you arrive and sending a digital copy later to get their signature on paper.\n\n### 5. Close for Signature\nThe contract includes the seller's name, the suggested price, commission terms (such as a six-month agreement), and is signed and ready for the seller to sign.\n\n\nREMINDER: You MUST include the sources above in your response to the user using markdown hyperlinks."}]},"uuid":"1b86d55a-0b64-48ff-b4b8-30c70bdcd667","timestamp":"2026-03-07T02:45:03.547Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"be9a9995-2503-41ba-9183-b62c4e487506"}

Daily Routines & Time-Blocking\n\n**The Power Hour:** MAPS coaches encourage agents to participate in a daily \"Power Hour\" from 9:00 AM to 10:00 AM, focused solely on lead generation. However, the broader KW philosophy (from Gary Keller's *The ONE Thing*) advocates for a **four-hour time block** each morning dedicated to your single most important activity -- for most agents, that means lead generation.\n\n**Time-Blocking Philosophy:** Time blocking is the underlying foundation of the KW business model. Agents are taught to set an appointment with themselves on their calendar for their ONE Thing. Gary Keller personally blocks the first four hours of every day: \"If you want to do something at the highest level, it's got to be four hours a day. Time on the task over time -- that's how you become a master at what matters most.\"\n\n**The 80/20 Rule:** Coaches help agents identify which 20% of their actions produce 80% of their results, then help them allocate more time to those high-value activities.\n\n**Ideal Day Structure:**\n- Morning: Lead generation is always the first and most protected time block\n- Lead generation is treated as the single most dollar-productive activity\n- Admin, appointments, and other tasks are scheduled around -- never during -- the lead gen block\n\n### 2. Lead Generation Methods\n\nKW teaches a comprehensive array of lead generation methods through the **Lead Generation 36:12:3** course (36 transactions, 12 months, 3 hours daily lead gen):\n\n- **Sphere of Influence / Database:** The single most emphasized source. For every 12 people in your \"Met\" database that you contact 33 times per year, expect 2 sales (1 repeat, 1 referral). Client Relationship & Referral Systems\n\n- **33 Touch Campaign:** 33 annual touches to maintain relationships and generate repeat/referral business\n- **8x8 Campaign:** 8 touches over 8 weeks to establish new relationships\n- **Never Ending Referrals Program:** Dedicated MAPS coaching program for systematizing database value through quarterly conversations and \"44X\" touches\n- **Referral Mastery System:** Permission-based marketing referral strategies rooted in generosity and appreciation, led by Michael J. Contract negotiation.\n\n**The 75% Rule:** 75% of each working day should be spent on income-producing activities: prospecting, lead follow-up, prequalifying, listing presentations, showing property, and negotiating contracts.\n\n**Schedule Philosophy:** \"If you limit the amount of time you work, you force yourself to be effective in the time that you do work.\" The schedule is designed to prevent agents from filling time with non-productive activities.\n\n### 2. Lead Generation Methods\n\nMike Ferry's system is **overwhelmingly focused on proactive prospecting** and de-emphasizes passive marketing:\n\n- **Expired Listings:** Primary prospecting source -- call and visit 5 expireds daily\n- **FSBOs (For Sale By Owners):** Primary prospecting source -- visit 5 FSBOs daily at their doors\n- **Past Clients / Center of Influence:** Contact every 90 days by phone + quarterly mailing. 40% of lifetime earnings should come from this source.\n- **Just Listed / Just Sold Circle Prospecting:** Calling/knocking around new listings and recent sales\n- **Door Knocking (Cold Doors):** The 30-Day Superstar Plan prescribes 10 cold doors per day, 5 days/week\n- **Cold Calling:** 10 cold calls per day, 5 days/week (Superstar Plan)\n- **Geographic Farming:** Calling and door-knocking around a designated farm area\n- **Absentee Owners:** Scripts for contacting non-resident property owners\n- **Renters / First-Time Homebuyers:** Dedicated scripts\n- **Notices of Default:** Scripts for distressed property owners\n- **Open Houses:** Prospecting at and around open houses\n\n**Anti-Marketing Stance:** Mike Ferry is known for his skepticism toward social media and passive marketing. He believes prospecting (direct human contact) is the ONLY way to develop skills for long-term business, and that social media's ROI is difficult to measure. He favors phone and in-person prospecting over digital channels.\n\n### 3. Scripts & Dialogues\n\nThe Mike Ferry Script Book is one of the most comprehensive in the industry, containing scripts for virtually every prospecting scenario:\n\n**Complete Script Categories:**\n- New to Real Estate / New to a Brokerage\n- Remind Them You're in Real Estate\n- New to the Area\n- Calling for Referrals\n- Center of Influence / Past Client Script\n- Calling Around Just Listed & Just Sold Properties\n- Prospecting at Open Houses\n- Powerful Closes for Prospecting\n- Calling & Door Knocking Around Farm Area\n- Contacting FSBOs (\"The Classic\" FSBO Script)\n- Contacting Absentee Owners\n- Calling Renters and First-Time Home Buyers\n- Prospecting Tenant-Occupied Listings\n- Calling on Notices of Default\n- Calling on Expireds\n- Resort Property Script\n- Pre-Qualifying the Listing Presentation Script\n- CMA Presentation Script\n- Listing Presentation Script\n- Handling Objections Scripts (40+ objections addressed)\n- Buyer Agent Scripts\n\n**Key Psychological Techniques in Scripts:**\n- \"Objection preemption\" (e.g., \"I know I'm probably catching you in the middle of something\")\n- Using the word \"And\" instead of \"But\" when transitioning into objection handling\n- Conducting \"surveys\" as a non-threatening opener for FSBOs\n- Always asking who else they know who might need real estate services\n\n### 4. Prospecting Systems\n\n**Daily Contact Goals:**\n- Minimum 3 hours of prospecting per day (phone or doors)\n- 10-12 contacts per hour of dialing = approximately 25-36 contacts per day\n- Visit 5 Expireds at their doors daily\n- Visit 5 FSBOs at their doors daily\n- 30 minutes daily for lead follow-up (possibly twice daily)\n- Set 1 qualified appointment per day\n- **Weekly target:** 120 phone answers = 5 future leads = 1 appointment\n\n**The \"Rule of Three\" (Contact Breakdown):**\n- If making 21 contacts/day: first 7 cover personal expenses, second 7 achieve business goals, third 7 fund dreams and aspirations\n\n**Follow-Up Cadence:**\n- Hot leads: Call morning, noon, and night on the same day\n- Database contacts: Every 90 days by phone + quarterly mailing\n- New leads: Aggressive, immediate follow-up -- the most aggressive agent wins\n\n**Daily Tracking Form:** Agents track contacts daily broken into categories: Center of Influence, Expireds, FSBOs, and others for each day of the week, plus leads generated, hours worked, appointments set, listings taken, and income earned.\n\n### 5. Marketing Strategies\n\nMike Ferry's marketing philosophy is fundamentally different from most coaching platforms:\n\n- **Prospecting IS the marketing:** Ferry believes 80% of your business should come from \"finding it\" through direct prospecting\n- **The Marketing Plan:** Mailings to past clients and sphere of influence with reports, property values, market statistics, legislation updates, and housing tips\n- **Just Listed / Just Sold postcards:** Used to generate conversations in geographic areas\n- **CMA packets:** Sent in advance of listing presentations with completed CMA, net sheet, and pre-completed contract\n- **Anti-social-media stance:** Ferry questions the ROI of social media, believing face-to-face and phone conversations are far more effective\n- **Minimal emphasis on video, digital ads, or content marketing:** The system is intentionally built around direct human interaction\n\n### 7. Client Relationship & Referral Systems\n\n- **Past Client / Center of Influence Database:** Treated as a personal \"gold mine\"\n- **The 10% Rule:** 10% of database contacts will generate business annually simply because you're asking\n- **Contact Frequency:** Every person in database contacted every 90 days by phone + quarterly mailing\n- **Database Size Goals:** Build to 500-1,000 names as quickly as possible\n- **Referral Script:** Ask contacts who they know who would like to buy or sell in the next 7-10 days; ask about their church group, family, neighborhood, and office\n- **Value-Add Mailings:** Send reports, property values, market statistics, legislation, and housing tips so contacts think of you for anything home-related\n- **40% Target:** 40% of lifetime earnings should come from past clients and center of influence\n\n### 8. Transaction Management\n\n**The 5-Step Listing Process:**\n1. Prequalify 100% of prospects 100% of the time, no exceptions\n2. Deliver a compelling listing presentation (with advance CMA packet)\n3. Present the CMA with pricing strategy, walking the seller through comparisons\n4. Close for the signature (have the contract pre-completed)\n5. Serve the listing and get it sold\n\n**Pre-Qualification Protocol:**\n- Done by phone before the listing appointment\n- Uncovers seller motivations, identifies challenges\n- Sets minimum standards for clients the agent will work with\n- Key question: \"If what I say makes sense and you feel comfortable, are you planning to list with me?\"\n- Identifies objections in advance so the agent is prepared\n\n**Team Structure Recommendations:**\n- Start with one production agent + one admin assistant\n- Add a transaction coordinator as volume grows\n- Eventually add a buyer's agent (paid at max 50% commission if leads furnished)\n- Warning against hiring too fast -- \"hiring one assistant each and two buyer's agents too quickly is financial disaster\"\n\n### 9. Goal Setting Frameworks\n\n**Mike Ferry's Goal Setting System:**\n1. Write out in detail what you want to achieve\n2. List all obstacles and solutions to those obstacles\n3. Set deadlines for all steps\n4. Build a schedule that supports the goals\n5. Identify the numbers that make it happen (hours, contacts, appointments, listings)\n6. Review your history and set goals to exceed past performance\n\n**Business Plan Components:**\n- A look at your history\n- Goals for the coming year\n- A schedule to support those goals\n- The numbers that make it happen\n- Problems and concerns with solutions\n- Duplicating and improving sources from last year\n\n**Reverse Engineering from Transaction Goals:**\n- Determine annual transaction goal\n- Calculate required monthly listings taken (e.g., 2 saleable listings/month)\n- Calculate required weekly appointments\n- Calculate required daily contacts (e.g., 25/day)\n- Calculate required prospecting hours (3 hours/day)\n\n### 10. Key Differentiators\n\n- **Founded 1975:** One of the oldest and most established real estate coaching programs\n- **Pure sales/prospecting focus:** Intentionally \"traditional\" -- no tech gimmicks, no social media emphasis\n- **High-accountability, no-nonsense culture:** More aggressive than competitors like Buffini; agents seeking strong prodding prefer MFO\n- **Script mastery:** Perhaps the most comprehensive real estate script library in the industry\n- **Mike Ferry personally involved:** Teaches at retreats, records Mornings with Mike, sets the tone\n- **Coaches are practicing agents:** All coaches are very successful Realtors themselves\n- **2,550,000+ personalized coaching calls** delivered across the organization's history\n- **Named NAR's Most Influential Real Estate Coach**\n- **Tom Ferry connection:** Tom Ferry (Mike's son) branched off with a more modern/tech-friendly approach; Mike Ferry represents the \"old school\" foundation\n\n### 11. Recommended Weekly Schedule\n\n**The Mike Ferry Daily Schedule (Monday-Friday):**\n| Time | Activity |\n|------|----------|\n| 6:00-7:00 AM | Wake up, exercise, stretch, healthy breakfast, affirmations |\n| 7:00-7:30 AM | Commute (media-free) |\n| 7:30-8:00 AM | Arrive at office, check messages, review Expireds/FSBOs, prep prospect lists |\n| 8:00-11:00 AM | Prospecting by phone (25-36 contacts) |\n| 11:00-11:30 AM | Lead follow-up (30 min) |\n| 11:30-12:00 PM | Role-play / script practice |\n| 12:00-1:00 PM | Lunch / break |\n| 1:00-2:30 PM | Listing appointment #1 |\n| 2:30-3:00 PM | Prep for next appointment |\n| 3:00-4:30 PM | Listing appointment #2 |\n| 4:30-5:00 PM | Admin, paperwork, update tracking forms |\n\n**The 30-Day Superstar Plan (for new agents or agents in a slump):**\n- 10 cold doors per day, 5 days/week for 4 weeks\n- 10 cold calls per day, 5 days/week for 4 weeks\n- Script practice daily\n\n### 12. Success Metrics / KPIs\n\n**Daily Tracking (Per Person Productivity Report):**\n- Hours of prospecting\n- Number of contacts (broken by source: COI, Expireds, FSBOs, other)\n- Leads generated\n- Appointments set\n\n**Weekly Targets:**\n- 120 phone answers = 5 future leads = 1 appointment\n- 15 hours of prospecting minimum\n\n**Monthly Targets:**\n- 2 saleable listings taken per month\n- 4 listings sold / buyer-controlled sales per month (minimum)\n\n**Conversion Ratios to Track:**\n- Call-to-contact ratio\n- Contact-to-lead ratio\n- Lead-to-appointment ratio (aim for 5%)\n- Appointment-to-listing ratio (aim for 70-80% with proper prequalifying)\n- Listing-to-sold ratio\n\n**Annual Benchmarks:**\n- Top coaching clients report 45-57+ transactions/year\n- Income doubling is commonly reported within first year of coaching\n- Track year-over-year improvement on all metrics\n\n---\n\n## SIDE-BY-SIDE COMPARISON\n\n| Dimension | KW MAPS / BOLD | Mike Ferry Organization
